title: "England v India: third men’s cricket Test, day four – live"
date: "2025-07-13T17:09:59.000Z"
slug: "england-v-india:-third-men's-cricket-test-day-four-live"
source: "Sport | The Guardian"
original_link: "https://www.theguardian.com/sport/live/2025/jul/13/england-v-india-third-mens-cricket-test-day-four-live"
description: "Updates from the day’s play at Lord’s  Pressure mounts on Australia top order  Jasprit Bumrah from the Nursery End… sizzling atmosphere here at Lord’s. Duckett continues his perky start by clipping for a single to get off strike. Right, Bumrah vs Crawley take two. Here we go! Chance! Ouch! Bumrah gets one to spit off a good length and it slams into Crawley’s left hand, that came out of nowhere! The ball flies up off the glove and Bumrah hares after the looping Dukes for the return catch. He doesn’t quite get there, a finger end on it as it drops to the turf. Great drama. Crawley could not do anything about that, no histrionics needed, that would have hurt. This fourth day pitch is starting to offer up some spice too.  Continue reading..."

It was given not out on the field but it looked pretty plum, Siraj certainly thought so and he implored his captain to send it upstairs. depart.</p>&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;239ba91f-a94d-4797-a828-e9b57302bc3d&quot;},{&quot;displayCredit&quot;:true,&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.ImageBlockElement&quot;,&quot;role&quot;:&quot;inline&quot;,&quot;media&quot;:{&quot;allImages&quot;:[{&quot;index&quot;:0,&quot;fields&quot;:{&quot;height&quot;:&quot;2246&quot;,&quot;width&quot;:&quot;3369&quot;},&quot;mediaType&quot;:&quot;Image&quot;,&quot;mimeType&quot;:&quot;image/jpeg&quot;,&quot;url&quot;:&quot;https://media.guim.co.uk/9b1c8b03602151cdfa863d499fa3aec06d3948ea/0_0_3369_2246/3369.jpg&quot;},{&quot;index&quot;:1,&quot;fields&quot;:{&quot;isMaster&quot;:&quot;true&quot;,&quot;height&quot;:&quot;2246&quot;,&quot;width&quot;:&quot;3369&quot;},&quot;mediaType&quot;:&quot;Image&quot;,&quot;mimeType&quot;:&quot;image/jpeg&quot;,&quot;url&quot;:&quot;https://media.guim.co.uk/9b1c8b03602151cdfa863d499fa3aec06d3948ea/0_0_3369_2246/master/3369.jpg&quot;},{&quot;index&quot;:2,&quot;fields&quot;:{&quot;height&quot;:&quot;1333&quot;,&quot;width&quot;:&quot;2000&quot;},&quot;mediaType&quot;:&quot;Image&quot;,&quot;mimeType&quot;:&quot;image/jpeg&quot;,&quot;url&quot;:&quot;https://media.guim.co.uk/9b1c8b03602151cdfa863d499fa3aec06d3948ea/0_0_3369_2246/2000.jpg&quot;},{&quot;index&quot;:3,&quot;fields&quot;:{&quot;height&quot;:&quot;667&quot;,&quot;width&quot;:&quot;1000&quot;},&quot;mediaType&quot;:&quot;Image&quot;,&quot;mimeType&quot;:&quot;image/jpeg&quot;,&quot;url&quot;:&quot;https://media.guim.co.uk/9b1c8b03602151cdfa863d499fa3aec06d3948ea/0_0_3369_2246/1000.jpg&quot;},{&quot;index&quot;:4,&quot;fields&quot;:{&quot;height&quot;:&quot;333&quot;,&quot;width&quot;:&quot;500&quot;},&quot;mediaType&quot;:&quot;Image&quot;,&quot;mimeType&quot;:&quot;image/jpeg&quot;,&quot;url&quot;:&quot;https://media.guim.co.uk/9b1c8b03602151cdfa863d499fa3aec06d3948ea/0_0_3369_2246/500.jpg&quot;},{&quot;index&quot;:5,&quot;fields&quot;:{&quot;height&quot;:&quot;93&quot;,&quot;width&quot;:&quot;14 Ollie Pope lbw b Mohammed Siraj 4 (England 42-2)&quot;,&quot;contributors&quot;:[],&quot;primaryDateLine&quot;:&quot;Sun 13 Jul 2025 18.11 BST&quot;,&quot;secondaryDateLine&quot;:&quot;First published on Sun 13 Jul 2025 10.15 BST&quot;},{&quot;id&quot;:&quot;6873899c8f08a97237f2dbf0&quot;,&quot;elements&quot;:[{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.TextBlockElement&quot;,&quot;html&quot;:&quot;<p>It’s all kicking off! Duckett scoops Siraj for four over the keeper’s head but the bowler gets his revenge and then some! Duckett goes to pull but the ball but it beats him for pace and he plinks an easy catch to mid-on. Siraj gives the pint sized batter a full serve and there’s even a little shoulder barge for afters! It is Ben Duckett c Bumrah b Mohammed Siraj 12 (England 22-1)</p></a></li><li><a href="https://www.theguardian.com/sport/live/2025/jul/13/england-v-india-third-mens-cricket-test-day-four-live?filterKeyEvents=false&amp;page=with%3Ablock-6871166c8f08a97237f2ccad#block-6871166c8f08a97237f2ccad" data-link-name="key event card | 17 of 18"><p><gu-island name="RelativeTime" priority="enhancement" deferuntil="visible" props="{&quot;then&quot;:1752398116000,&quot;now&quot;:1752426660000,&quot;editionId&quot;:&quot;INT&quot;}"><time datetime="2025-07-13T09:15:16.000Z" data-locale="en-gb" title="Sunday, 13 July 2025 at 10:15 British Summer Time">8h ago</time></gu-island></p><p>Preamble</p></a></li></ul></div></gu-island><gu-island name="FilterKeyEventsToggle" priority="feature" deferuntil="visible" props="{&quot;filterKeyEvents&quot;:false,&quot;id&quot;:&quot;filter-toggle-mobile&quot;}"><span id="filter-toggle-mobile"></span><p><label id="src-component-104629_description" data-component="filter-key-events" data-link-name="filter-key-events-on">Show key events only<p><span>Please turn on JavaScript to use this feature</span></p></label></p></gu-island></span></p><article id="block-6873e8768f088b778dd2a64a"><header><h2>Gill is not out!</h2></header><p>Shubman Gill knew he hadn’t hit the ball. In fact this is a rare shocker from Paul Reiffel. Gill tried to drive another very full delivery from Carse, missed and was caught by Jamie Smith. Replays showed daylight between bat and ball.</p></article><article id="block-6873e8548f08a97237f2df39"><header><h2>Gill given out but reviews immediately!</h2></header><p><strong>Oh, the tension.</strong></p></article><article id="block-6873e76e8f08a97237f2df2c"><header></header><p><strong>14th over: India 47-2 (Rahul 29, Gill 2)</strong> Stokes boots the bowling crease angrily in anger after starting with a four-ball on the hips of KL Rahul. The rest of the over is spot on – five dot balls in a row including one delivery that bursts past Rahul’s attempted cut.</p><p>Time for four or five more overs tonight.</p></article><article id="block-6873e6bf8f08755807c82e07"><header></header><p><strong>13th over: India 43-2 (Rahul 25, Gill 2) </strong>With everyone expecting a short ball first up, Carse starts with a yorker length outswinger that beats Gill. England’s fielders are flapping their gums incessantly, an inevitable and compelling response to last night’s contretemps.</p><p>Gill, beaten again second ball, leans into a pristine extra cover drive to get off the mark. Those two runs mean he has broken Rahul Dravid’s record for most runs in a series by an Indian batter in England: 603 runs and counting.</p></article><article id="block-6873e6428f08755807c82e05"><header></header><p><strong>A misfield from Stokes in the covers gave Rahul a single.</strong> It was a blessing in disguise: two balls later Karun Nair offered no stroke to a straight one from Carse and was palpably LBW. No hesitation from the umpire, no review from Nair – he knew it was a fatal misjudgement.</p><p>With half an hour to play, Shubman Gill walks out to a lively reception. What goes around comes around. The next 30 minutes could be spectacular.</p></article><article id="block-6873e6138f08755807c82e04"><header><h2>WICKET! India 41-2 (Nair LBW b Carse 14)</h2></header><p>Ben Stokes is so good that even his misfields can lead to a wicket.</p><figure id="42d1cd0b-f63b-4f27-bbbd-e011e23aec51" data-spacefinder-role="inline" data-spacefinder-type="model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.ImageBlockElement"><div id="img-2"><picture><source srcset="https://i.guim.co.uk/img/media/495060bd2b0195794bdb134a0b0132a441748f04/0_0_4286_2906/master/4286.jpg?width=700&amp;dpr=2&amp;s=none&amp;crop=none" media="(min-width: 660px) and (-webkit-min-device-pixel-ratio: 1.25), (min-width: 660px) and (min-resolution: 120dpi)"><source srcset="https://i.guim.co.uk/img/media/495060bd2b0195794bdb134a0b0132a441748f04/0_0_4286_2906/master/4286.jpg?width=700&amp;dpr=1&amp;s=none&amp;crop=none" media="(min-width: 660px)"><source srcset="https://i.guim.co.uk/img/media/495060bd2b0195794bdb134a0b0132a441748f04/0_0_4286_2906/master/4286.jpg?width=465&amp;dpr=2&amp;s=none&amp;crop=none" media="(min-width: 320px) and (-webkit-min-device-pixel-ratio: 1.25), (min-width: 320px) and (min-resolution: 120dpi)"><source srcset="https://i.guim.co.uk/img/media/495060bd2b0195794bdb134a0b0132a441748f04/0_0_4286_2906/master/4286.jpg?width=465&amp;dpr=1&amp;s=none&amp;crop=none" media="(min-width: 320px)"><img alt="Brydon Carse appeals successfully for the lbw wicket of Karun Nair." src="https://i.guim.co.uk/img/media/495060bd2b0195794bdb134a0b0132a441748f04/0_0_4286_2906/master/4286.jpg?width=465&amp;dpr=1&amp;s=none&amp;crop=none" width="465" height="315.2799813345777" loading="lazy"></picture></div><figcaption data-spacefinder-role="inline"><span><svg width="18" height="13" viewBox="0 0 18 13"><path d="M18 3.5v8l-1.5 1.5h-15l-1.5-1.5v-8l1.5-1.5h3.5l2-2h4l2 2h3.5l1.5 1.5zm-9 7.5c1.9 0 3.5-1.6 3.5-3.5s-1.6-3.5-3.5-3.5-3.5 1.6-3.5 3.5 1.6 3.5 3.5 3.5z"></path></svg></span><span>Brydon Carse appeals successfully for the lbw wicket of Karun Nair.</span> Photograph: Peter Cziborra/Action Images/Reuters</figcaption></figure></article><article id="block-6873e52d8f08755807c82dff"><header></header><p><strong>12th over: India 40-1 (Rahul 24, Nair 14) </strong>Another accurate over from Stokes, who is whacking the pitch and making the batters play at as many deliveries as possible. One run from it.</p><p>“A five-day match doesn’t hinge on a single moment but man, that Woakes drop feels defining for several reasons,” says Max Williams. “Reckon there’s any way back for Ollie Robsinson or has that ship sailed?”</p><p>Sadly, I think it has sailed. He’s got 86 wickets at 22.92, and he had fitness issues in maybe a quarter of those games. Grrrrrrrrr.</p></article><article id="block-6873e3e38f08a97237f2df18"><header></header><p><strong>11th over: India 39-1 (Rahul 23, Nair 14) </strong>Woakes gives way to Brydon Carse, whose first over includes four singles and a cracking yorker that is defended expertly by Rahul. He has been a problem for England throughout the series; he’s becoming an even bigger one in this run-chase. If India are still one down at the close they will be heavy favourites.</p></article><article id="block-6873e21b8f08755807c82df1"><header><h2>Drinks: India need 158 more runs to win</h2></header><p><strong>10th over: India 35-1 (Rahul 21, Nair 12) </strong>Stokes comes on for archer, whose new-ball spell of 4-0-18-1 wasn’t the best. His first delivery is a no-ball; his first legal delivery is thick edged for four by Rahul.</p><p>You feel England need at least one more wicket tonight – and that Stokes is most likely to provide it. He starts to pummel a hard length and beats Rahul with a vicious seaming lifter. Time for drinks.</p></article><article id="block-6873e0da8f08755807c82de3"><header></header><p><strong>9th over: India 30-1 (Rahul 17, Nair 12) </strong>Karun Nair has started well; he looks solid in defence and certain in his shot selection.</p><p>Ben Stokes is getting loose so he should be bowling soon. Match situations like this were invited for him.</p><p>“When I look back to that 2018 Indian tour, I think about how Sam Curran was England’s player of the series, and how Kohli said he was the difference between the two teams,” says Matt Emerson. “His Test career never really kicked on after that, did it?”</p><p>That’s an understatement. From memory he batted very well on the Total <a href="https://www.theguardian.com/sport/cricket" data-link-name="in body link" data-component="auto-linked-tag">Cricket</a> tour of Sri Lanka the same year and also played an important with the ball in South Africa just before Covid. It’s a complicated case: lotta ins, lotta outs, lotta what-have-yous. He’s got the competitive instinct of a Bazballer but not the skill set; it’s hard to see getting a game under this regime unless he becomes a regular top six batter.</p></article><article id="block-6873dff18f08755807c82ddc"><header></header><p><strong>8th over: India 28-1 (Rahul 17, Nair 10) </strong>Archer continues – and starts with another very full ball that Nair pushes into the off side. The ball isn’t swinging so Archer’s plan isn’t clear.</p><p>When he hits a good length, with the occasional short delivery, he looks a much bigger threat. Just one run from the over.</p></article><article id="block-6873df1e8f088b778dd2a60b"><header></header><p><strong>7th over: India 27-1 (Rahul 17, Nair 9) </strong>Archer usually prefers the Pavilion End at Lord’s, which is where Woakes is bowling. That’s because the ball bounced viciously this morning when Bumrah was at the Nursery End so England want Archer to have a similar impact. But perhaps they are getting too cute; by all accounts it’s not easy to change ends at Lord’s given the impact of the slope. You could bowl Carse from the Nursery End, then bring Archer back when Woakes finishes his spell.</p><p>Nair leans into a cover drive off Woakes that is excellently stopped by the diving Pope; that surely saved three runs.</p></article><article id="block-6873ddf98f08a97237f2defa"><header></header><p><strong>6th over: India 26-1 (Rahul 17, Nair 8) </strong>A poor ball from Archer, way too full, is driven handsomely through the covers by Nair for India’s third boundary in four balls. Although he took a key early wicket, Archer has been quite poor in this spell – his length has been far too full.</p><p>It happens again later in the over when a half-volley is timed beautifully to the cover boundary by Rahul. Archer signals to Stokes that he wants a cover sweeper; Stokes declines.</p></article><article id="block-6873dd1d8f088b778dd2a603"><header></header><p><strong>5th over: India 17-1 (Rahul 13, Nair 4) </strong>The plot thickens: <strong>Woakes has dropped Rahul</strong> off his own bowling! Rahul clothed an outswinger back towards Woakes, who reached to his left in his follow through but couldn’t hang on. Woakes is such a good fielder and there was a gasp of surprise when he put it down.</p><p>Rahul adds to Woakes’s pain by hitting the next two balls through point for four, one of each foot. If the first, played off the back foot, was elegant, the second was struck with sadistic intent. <strong>India need another 176 runs to win.</strong></p><figure id="28612120-1718-40b2-a5e7-9982ccdc7eb2" data-spacefinder-role="inline" data-spacefinder-type="model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.ImageBlockElement"><div id="img-3"><picture><source dismiss KL Rahul of India.</span> Photograph: Clive Mason/Getty Images</figcaption></figure></article><article id="block-6873dbf98f08a97237f2deec"><header></header><p><strong>4th over: India 9-1 (Rahul 5, Nair 4) </strong>A full inswinger from Archer is timed nicely through mid-on for two by Nair. Not sure that’s the length to bowl to him.</p><p><em>That’s</em> the length. Nair ducks into a short ball that thumps him just below the left shoulder. The follow-up ball doesn’t come out right and turns into a full toss that is forced through mid-off for two more. Terrific cricket.</p></article><article id="block-6873db548f088b778dd2a5f3"><header></header><p><strong>3rd over: India 5-1 (Rahul 5, Nair 0) </strong>Rahul pads up to an inducker from Woakes that misses the off stump by a micrometre. That was close. Closer than close, but this is no time for Rosie Gaines lyrics.</p><p>England are all over India with the new ball. Woakes has a big LBW appeal turned down against Rahul; it didn’t have much going for it, in truth, but you can understand why England got carried away. This is tense!</p><p>“Was there any point in making our No11 bat, especially when we will be relying on him to spin the Indians out soon?” asks Rob Lewis. “Shouldn’t his hand have been protected from further damage?”</p><p>If it was his bowling hand then maybe, but it’s his left hand so I’m not sure it makes much difference. And those seven runs he added with Jofra Archer could be the difference between rotten eggs and a knighthood.</p><p>Okay I’m getting carried away. But this is tense!</p></article><article id="block-6873da788f08755807c82da1"><header></header><p><strong>2nd over: India 5-1 (Rahul 5, Nair 0) </strong>Jaiswal was on strike because KL Rahul had clipped four off the pads and then pulled a single.</p><p>Kumar Sangakkara, commentating on Sky, says Jaiswal’s concentration didn’t look right throughout his short innings. His dismissal came from a particularly ill-judged stroke, a hook at a ball that was too high, too wide – and the first delivery he’d faced from Archer in the innings.</p></article><article id="block-6873d92e8f088b778dd2a5e2"><header><h2>WICKET! India 5-1 (Jaiswal c Smith b Archer 0)</h2></header><p>Jofra Archer strikes fourth ball! Yashasvi Jaiswal played a horrible hook that went miles in the air and was calmly caught by Jamie Smith. That was the first ball he faced from Archer in this innings, which makes their burgeoning head-to-head record a little one-sided: four balls, two wickets, no runs.</p><figure id="fbfe50b1-1336-46ae-8a6a-d235bc3da717" data-spacefinder-role="inline" data-spacefinder-type="model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.ImageBlockElement"><div id="img-1"><picture><source Jaiswal of India.</span> Photograph: Gareth Copley/Getty Images</figcaption></figure></article><article id="block-6873d8b98f08a97237f2dec4"><header></header><p><strong>1st over: India 0-0 (Jaiswal 0, Rahul 0) </strong>Woakes goes straight around the wicket to Jaiswal, beating him with successive deliveries just outside off stump. Lovely line.</p><p>The fourth ball, left by Jaiswal, bounces twice before reaching Smith. An excellent start from Woakes, whose first over on Friday was panelled for 13 by Jaiswal.</p><p>“Talking of (un)true newspaper headlines,” says Simon McMahon it’s often reported that, upon the sinking of the Titanic, the front page of the Dundee Courier – or the Press &amp; Journal in Aberdeen, neither renowned as internationalist in outlook – carried the headline ‘North East Man Lost at Sea’.</p><p>“A bit like saying ‘Leach Defies Australia to Guide England Home’ after Headingley 2019.</p></article><article id="block-6873d8678f088b778dd2a5cd"><header></header><p><strong>Chris Woakes will start from the Pavilion End.</strong> If this goes badly, he could feasibly be playing his last Test.</p></article><article id="block-6873d8018f08a97237f2deb5"><header></header><p><strong>The WinViz verdict</strong></p><ul>
 <li>
  <p><strong>India</strong> 76 per cent</p></li>
 <li>
  <p><strong>England</strong> 24 per cent</p></li>
</ul><p>My instinct, largely worthless, is that England’s chances of victory are closer to 35-40 per cent. We’ll soon find out.</p></article><article id="block-6873d7738f08755807c82d86"><header></header><p><strong>There will be time for around 18 overs tonight.</strong> Here’s the deal. If England are to win this game, they have to take wickets plural in that time.</p></article><article id="block-6873d57a8f08a97237f2de9d"><header><h2>WICKET! England 192 all out (Bashir b Washington 2)</h2></header><p>That’s all she wrote. Washington Sundar skids one past Bashir, who becomes the seventh England player to be bowled in this innings and the 12th in the match.</p><p>Washington, the quiet achiever of this team, has triggered an England collapse of six wickets for just 38 runs. Ouch. <strong>India need 193 to win.</strong></p><figure id="a860c03d-e19a-432b-a23a-38e507d16703" data-spacefinder-role="inline" data-spacefinder-type="model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.ImageBlockElement"><div id="img-5"><picture><source srcset="https://i.guim.co.uk/img/media/5cdd6889bf90eeecf0d0c3f3362f419513ba88b2/0_0_4152_2768/master/4152.jpg?width=700&amp;dpr=2&amp;s=none&amp;crop=none" media="(min-width: 660px) and (-webkit-min-device-pixel-ratio: 1.25), (min-width: 660px) and (min-resolution: 120dpi)"><source srcset="https://i.guim.co.uk/img/media/5cdd6889bf90eeecf0d0c3f3362f419513ba88b2/0_0_4152_2768/master/4152.jpg?width=700&amp;dpr=1&amp;s=none&amp;crop=none" media="(min-width: 660px)"><source loading="lazy"></picture></div><figcaption data-spacefinder-role="inline"><span><svg width="18" height="13" viewBox="0 0 18 13"><path d="M18 3.5v8l-1.5 1.5h-15l-1.5-1.5v-8l1.5-1.5h3.5l2-2h4l2 2h3.5l1.5 1.5zm-9 7.5c1.9 0 3.5-1.6 3.5-3.5s-1.6-3.5-3.5-3.5-3.5 1.6-3.5 3.5 1.6 3.5 3.5 3.5z"></path></svg></span><span>India's Akash Deep congratulates India's Washington Sundar (R) on taking the final England wicket.</span> Photograph: Ben Stansall/AFP/Getty Images</figcaption></figure></article><article id="block-6873d4848f08755807c82d78"><header></header><p><strong>62nd over: England 192-9 (Archer 5, Bashir 2) </strong>Eleven England players have been bowled in this Test, a remarkable statistic and the first time that has happened since the Cape Town Test of March/April 1906.</p><p>Bumrah tries to make it 12 but is repelled by Archer and Bashir. The sub keeper Jurel also saves four byes with a smart dive down the leg side. You wouldn’t know it from all the byes India have conceded, but he has kept quite beautifully.</p></article><article id="block-6873d3ba8f08a97237f2de87"><header></header><p><strong>61st over: England 191-9 (Archer 5, Bashir 1) </strong>Bashir thick edges Sundar’s first ball for a single to get off strike. The fourth innings of this game, while not quite make or break for Bashir, will be loaded with pressure. One bad spell could cost England the game; one good spell could win it. It’s a lot of responsibility on a 21-year-old.</p><p>Archer can’t return the favour, which means Bashir will be on strike at the start of Bumrah’s next over.</p></article><article id="block-6873d3128f08a97237f2de84"><header></header><p><strong>60th over: England 190-9 (Archer 5, Bashir 0) </strong>Archer turns down a single early in Bumrah’s over. It might be that he only does that at this end because of the threat and pace of Bumrah.</p><p>The last ball of the over, an attempted yorker that turns into a full toss, is punched through mid-off for four by Archer. Every little helps.</p><p>“Speaking just for myself from a sweaty north west the reason why India are heavy favourites, even before this clatter of wickets, is that their openers are in good nick and have consistently got them through the tough new-ball period,” says Will Vignoles. “England’s change bowlers have struggled to maintain pressure and they’re generally better players of spin. Also bar Pant also less likely to get out trying to slog sweep a guy bowling 85mph+. Maybe I’m just being a miserable git but even as a Bazball true believer this has been a bit disappointing from England. As well as India have bowled, this has felt a bit of a headloss. Am I being unfair?”</p><p>I can see both sides! One of the reason I’m reluctant to say we’re all doomed is that we were having the same conversation at this stage of <a href="https://www.espncricinfo.com/series/india-tour-of-england-2018-1119528/england-vs-india-1st-test-1119549/full-scorecard" data-link-name="in body link">the Edgbaston Test in 2018</a>. India’s target was almost identical and I’m not sure that pitch was worse than this.</p></article><article id="block-6873d20f8f08755807c82d64"><header></header><p><strong>59th over: England 186-9 (Archer 1, Bashir 0) </strong>“I do wish sometimes we didn’t live in this fast-paced fractured meme society,” writes Pete Salmon. “If ‘Mr Smith Goes to Washington’ had been splashed a newspaper headline in the 1980s we’d still be talking about it now.</p><p>“Reminds me of a fun book I had when I was young which had (according to it) true newspaper headlines, including the the winner of a World’s Most Boring Headline competition: Small Earthquake in Chile, Not Many Dead. That became a catchphrase in our family for a day of minor grievances, as in:</p><blockquote data-spacefinder-role="inline">
 <p><svg viewBox="0 0 22 14" style="fill:var(--block-quote-fill)"><path d="M5.255 0h4.75c-.572 4.53-1.077 8.972-1.297 13.941H0C.792 9.104 2.44 4.53 5.255 0Zm11.061 0H21c-.506 4.53-1.077 8.972-1.297 13.941h-8.686c.902-4.837 2.485-9.411 5.3-13.941Z"></path></svg>‘How was your day?’</p>
 <p>‘Oh you know, Small Earthquake in Chile, Not Many Dead’</p>
</blockquote><p>They won’t be saying that in the England dressing-room tonight.</p></article><article id="block-6873d1538f088b778dd2a595"><header></header><p><strong>58th over: England 185-9 (Archer 0, Bashir 0) </strong>Shoaib Bashir comes out at No11 despite a significant injury to his left hand. He wrings his hand in pain after doing very well to keep out another Bumrah yorker.</p><p>A wicket maiden from Bumrah, a bowler without compare.</p></article><article id="block-6873d0e48f08755807c82d5e"><header></header><p><strong>Chris Woakes walks off shaking his head, </strong>trying to fathom what just happened. He’s the sixth England batter to be out bowled in this innings. Bumrah got him with a huge breakback that brushed the inside-edge and rattled the bails.</p><p>Thirty seconds earlier Bumrah was sitting on his backside receiving treatment after landing awkwardly in his delivery stride. Then he got to his feet and bowled an 86mph off-break.</p></article><article id="block-6873d01c8f08a97237f2de6f"><header><h2>WICKET! England 185-9 (Woakes b Bumrah 10)</h2></header><p>Pure genius.</p></article><article id="block-6873cf628f08755807c82d52"><header></header><p><strong>57th over: England 185-8 (Woakes 10, Archer 0) </strong>Woakes drives Washington to long on for a single, the only run from an over filled with watchful defensive strokes.</p><p>Time is still a factor in this game. England would probably like just under about an hour with the ball tonight, as that would give Jofra Archer two spells with the new ball – one tonight and another in the morning.</p></article><article id="block-6873cf258f08755807c82d4d"><header></header><p><strong>56th over: England 184-8 (Woakes 9, Archer 0) </strong>Jofra Archer emerges from Bumrah’s over with his wicket intact, though I’m not entirely sure how. Bumrah’s skill is mind-blowing.</p></article><article id="block-6873cef68f08755807c82d49"><header></header><p><strong>Archer is not out! </strong>Yep, the ball sneaked under the bat, which then scraped the turf. India are down to their last review; I suspect they’ll get by.</p></article><article id="block-6873ce8e8f08a97237f2de5e"><header></header><p><strong>India review for caught behind against Archer</strong></p><p>The keeper Jurel leads the appeal for caught behind when Archer tries to drive a very full delivery outside off stump. It’s given not out and <strong>Gill reviews</strong> a little reluctantly. I think Archer’s bat scraped the ground.</p></article><article id="block-6873cda98f08755807c82d37"><header><h2>WICKET! England 182-8 (Carse b Bumrah 1)</h2></header><p>And it’s goodnight from Brydon Carse. He has just been bowled by a <em>perfect </em>yorker from Jasprit Bumrah, which pegged back the leg stump after sneaking under the bat.</p><p>Some of the England wickets today were eminently avoidable; not that one. It was a great delivery from an all-time great bowler. Absurdly, given how well he has bowled, it’s Bumrah’s first wicket of the innings.</p><figure id="fe236499-2cd7-4a26-9d7d-333c976198b3" data-spacefinder-role="inline" data-spacefinder-type="model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.ImageBlockElement"><div id="img-6"><picture><source srcset="https://i.guim.co.uk/img/media/b46a7c370084f2d3fa4ad11bd53eefd7c4f974bc/0_0_5024_3350/master/5024.jpg?width=700&amp;dpr=2&amp;s=none&amp;crop=none" media="(min-width: 660px) and (-webkit-min-device-pixel-ratio: 1.25), (min-width: 660px) and (min-resolution: 120dpi)"><source Photograph: Richard Pelham/AP</figcaption></figure></article><article id="block-6873cd5f8f08755807c82d36"><header></header><p><strong>55th over: England 181-7 (Woakes 8, Carse 1) </strong>Stokes had dragged a sweep for four earlier in the over, an effective but not particularly convincing shot.</p><p>“Hi Rob,” says Anthony Baxter. “Following on from Ray Murphy’s inspired reference, when Mr Smith finally makes it there, he encounters the crooked elder statesman Senator Paine, whose cricketing namesake also had a few, shall we say, bones in his closet.”</p></article><article id="block-6873cc738f08755807c82d31"><header><h2>WICKET! England 181-7 (Stokes b Washington 33)</h2></header><p>Washington Sundar has wiped out England’s middle order! Stokes threw everything into a slog sweep, missed and was cleaned up. He whacked his bat angrily before getting to his feet and stomping off furiously.</p><p>Not only has Washington dismissed Root, Stokes and Smith, he’s bowled all three of them.</p><figure id="090bf71c-a3d9-4e58-8f4d-f7c10e15cb8b" data-spacefinder-role="inline" data-spacefinder-type="model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.ImageBlockElement"><div id="img-7"><picture><source srcset="https://i.guim.co.uk/img/media/bb37e8ce73258de84c8e7dae8ea335be7d0c9c27/237_0_2368_1894/master/2368.jpg?width=700&amp;dpr=2&amp;s=none&amp;crop=none" media="(min-width: 660px) and (-webkit-min-device-pixel-ratio: 1.25), (min-width: 660px) and (min-resolution: 120dpi)"><source srcset="https://i.guim.co.uk/img/media/bb37e8ce73258de84c8e7dae8ea335be7d0c9c27/237_0_2368_1894/master/2368.jpg?width=700&amp;dpr=1&amp;s=none&amp;crop=none" media="(min-width: 660px)"><source srcset="https://i.guim.co.uk/img/media/bb37e8ce73258de84c8e7dae8ea335be7d0c9c27/237_0_2368_1894/master/2368.jpg?width=465&amp;dpr=2&amp;s=none&amp;crop=none" media="(min-width: 320px) and (-webkit-min-device-pixel-ratio: 1.25), (min-width: 320px) and (min-resolution: 120dpi)"><source srcset="https://i.guim.co.uk/img/media/bb37e8ce73258de84c8e7dae8ea335be7d0c9c27/237_0_2368_1894/master/2368.jpg?width=465&amp;dpr=1&amp;s=none&amp;crop=none" media="(min-width: 320px)"><img alt="England's captain Ben Stokes reacts as he walks off the field after losing his wicket." src="https://i.guim.co.uk/img/media/bb37e8ce73258de84c8e7dae8ea335be7d0c9c27/237_0_2368_1894/master/2368.jpg?width=465&amp;dpr=1&amp;s=none&amp;crop=none" width="465" height="371.92145270270265" loading="lazy"></picture></div><figcaption data-spacefinder-role="inline"><span><svg width="18" height="13" viewBox="0 0 18 13"><path d="M18 3.5v8l-1.5 1.5h-15l-1.5-1.5v-8l1.5-1.5h3.5l2-2h4l2 wicket.</span> Photograph: Richard Pelham/AP</figcaption></figure></article><article id="block-6873cba58f08a97237f2de50"><header></header><p><strong>54th over: England 177-6 (Stokes 29, Woakes 8) </strong>Jasprit Bumrah returns for a post-tea burst. He has a superb record against both these players, especially Woakes.</p><p>Stokes almost gets a taste of his own medicine when he survives a <strong>run-out chance</strong> to Gill at mid-off. The ball bounced perfectly into the hands of Gill, whose throw whistled past the stumps with the diving Stokes just short of his ground.</p></article><article id="block-6873cab98f088b778dd2a567"><header></header><p><strong>53rd over: England 176-6 (Stokes 28, Woakes 8) </strong>The dangerous Washington Sundar, who took 2 for 13 in seven overs before tea, resumes after the break. Stokes defends a series of deliveries before squirting a thick edge for as single. That takes him to 28 from 89 balls; a strike rate of 31 shows how responsibly Stokes has batted.</p></article><article id="block-6873c95c8f08755807c82d0d"><header></header><p>﻿<strong>“Afternoon Rob,”</strong> says Simon McMahon. “This Test match, being as delicately balanced as the atmosphere when you’re on the night bus to London with Francis Begbie and realise you’ve forgotten to bring the cairds, is an engrossing watch. And the blossoming rivalry that is Alcaraz v Sinner is just about to start in the Wimbledon men’s singles final. The next few hours could be <em>epic</em>.”</p><figure id="60a77241-de99-4806-a6bc-2d9d6f70e726" data-spacefinder-role="inline" data-spacefinder-type="model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.RichLinkBlockElement"><gu-island name="RichLinkComponent" priority="feature" deferuntil="idle" props="{&quot;richLinkIndex&quot;:1,&quot;element&quot;:{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.RichLinkBlockElement&quot;,&quot;prefix&quot;:&quot;Related: &quot;,&quot;text&quot;:&quot;Wimbledon 2025 men’s singles final: Jannik Sinner v Carlos Alcaraz – live&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;60a77241-de99-4806-a6bc-2d9d6f70e726&quot;,&quot;role&quot;:&quot;inline&quot;,&quot;url&quot;:&quot;https://www.theguardian.com/sport/live/2025/jul/13/wimbledon-mens-singles-final-jannik-sinner-carlos-alcaraz-live-tennis&quot;},&quot;ajaxUrl&quot;:&quot;https://api.nextgen.guardianapps.co.uk&quot;,&quot;format&quot;:{&quot;design&quot;:11,&quot;display&quot;:0,&quot;theme&quot;:2}}"></gu-island></figure></article><article id="block-6873c7bf8f08755807c82cef"><header></header><p><strong>Teatime reading</strong></p><figure id="92191324-c99c-49e8-9b1c-33c3bd77810d" data-spacefinder-role="inline" data-spacefinder-type="model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.RichLinkBlockElement"><gu-island name="RichLinkComponent" priority="feature" deferuntil="idle" props="{&quot;richLinkIndex&quot;:1,&quot;element&quot;:{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.RichLinkBlockElement&quot;,&quot;prefix&quot;:&quot;Related: &quot;,&quot;text&quot;:&quot;Pressure mounts on Konstas and Khawaja as Australia collapse against West Indies&quot;,&quot;elementId&quot;:&quot;92191324-c99c-49e8-9b1c-33c3bd77810d&quot;,&quot;role&quot;:&quot;inline&quot;,&quot;url&quot;:&quot;https://www.theguardian.com/sport/2025/jul/13/west-indies-australia-third-test-day-one-report&quot;},&quot;ajaxUrl&quot;:&quot;https://api.nextgen.guardianapps.co.uk&quot;,&quot;format&quot;:{&quot;design&quot;:11,&quot;display&quot;:0,&quot;theme&quot;:2}}"></gu-island></figure></article><article id="block-6873c6f08f088b778dd2a539"><header></header><p><strong>Mr Smith goes to Washington</strong></p><p>Thanks for all the <s>fawning</s> nice emails about the above description of Jamie Smith’s wicket. Can I just reiterate that it’s <a href="https://www.theguardian.com/sport/live/2021/jan/15/australia-cricket-vs-india-fourth-test-live-2021-gabba-day-one-international-aus-v-ind-series-match-game-start-time-teams-latest-scores-updates?page=with%3Ablock-60010bbd8f08729f182884b1#block-60010bbd8f08729f182884b1" data-link-name="in body link">Ray Murphy’s line</a>, not mine? It’s far too classy and understated to have emerged from my brain.</p></article><article id="block-6873c5438f08a97237f2de02"><header><h2>Tea</h2></header><p><strong>52nd over: England 175-6 (Stokes 27, Woakes 8)</strong> Stokes pushes Jadeja between the legs of short leg, who didn’t have time to get down. Woakes is then beaten by a gorgeous delivery, much slower and bowled from wider on the crease.</p><p>This is <em>so</em> good, and there’s another two-and-a-half hours to come after tea. The match remains in the balance after another compelling session. England scored 77 in 27 overs for the loss of two wickets – but they were the wickets India wanted most, Joe Root and Jamie Smith.</p><p>The consensus is that India are fractionally ahead in the game. I think it’s closer than that.</p></article><article id="block-6873c4a98f088b778dd2a51b"><header></header><p><strong>51st over: England 173-6 (Stokes 26, Woakes 7) </strong>Stokes continues to defend almost solemnly against Washington. Every particle of his being is fighting to produce another Lord’s epic.</p><p>An accurate maiden ends with a good delivery that boings past the edge as Stokes goes back to defend.</p></article><article id="block-6873c3d28f08755807c82ccd"><header></header><p><strong>50th over: England 173-6 (Stokes 26, Woakes 7) </strong>Woakes is beaten by a horrible delivery from Jadeja, speared in, just short of a length, from round the wicket before straightening dramatically. Time for two more overs before tea.</p><p>“Congratulations!” says John Starbuck. “I bet you were kept awake last night pondering the possibility of ‘Mr Smith goes to Washington’, delighted to get the chance to use it, and hopeful of the Guardian’s Quotes of the Year options.”</p><p>No no, I can take no credit. A reader by the name of Ray Murphy coined the phrase (at least on these pages) when Washington dismissed Steve Smith in the 2020-21 Border/Gavaskar series. <a href="https://www.theguardian.com/sport/live/2021/jan/15/australia-cricket-vs-india-fourth-test-live-2021-gabba-day-one-international-aus-v-ind-series-match-game-start-time-teams-latest-scores-updates?page=with%3Ablock-60010bbd8f08729f182884b1#block-60010bbd8f08729f182884b1" data-link-name="in body link">And here’s the proof</a>.</p></article><article id="block-6873c3638f088b778dd2a514"><header></header><p><strong>49th over: England 170-6 (Stokes 25, Woakes 5) </strong>Woakes skips down to clip Washington between mid-on and midwicket for four. That’s a fine shot.</p><p>The ball is spitting, as you’d expect on a pitch that has been in the oven for nearly four days. It sounds like Shoaib Bashir will be able to bowl despite the injury to his left hand. He’ll surely bat too, even if it’s one-handed <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Qx4CcVR0CDQ" data-link-name="in body link">like Malcolm Marshall in 1984</a>.</p></article><article id="block-6873c3298f08a97237f2ddf5"><header></header><p><strong>48th over: England 165-6 (Stokes 24, Woakes 1) </strong>Maiden from Jadeja to Woakes.</p><p>Domink Hindal has shared an intriguing stat from Cricbuzz: since 2024, when playing the conventional sweep in Tests, Joe Root has scored 101 runs at an average of 17. I’d like to see the dismissals, and his sweeping stats before 2024, but an average that low suggests it’s not the safe shot many of us thought.</p></article><article id="block-6873c1b38f088b778dd2a50a"><header></header><p><strong>47th over: England 165-6 (Stokes 24, Woakes 1) </strong>There have been a number of dramatic momentum shifts in this brilliant Test match. We’re in the midst of another: England were 154 for 4 and eyeing 250+. Now they’re 165 for 6 and could struggle to reach 200.</p></article><article id="block-6873c1388f088b778dd2a503"><header></header><p><strong>England are in bother. </strong>Washington bowled Root round his legs and now he has done Smith on the outside. Smith pushed defensively down the wrong line and was mortified to see the ball go straight on to plink the off stump.</p><p>I’d like to see the replay again as there was probably some drift involved. Not that it matters: the big news is that Jamie Smith is out and India are into the bowlers.</p></article><article id="block-6873c1238f08a97237f2dde8"><header><h2>WICKET! England 164-6 (Smith b Washington 6)</h2></header><p>Mr Smith goes to Washington!</p><figure id="2147c3e2-4e17-41cf-b093-f62700ac68af" data-spacefinder-role="inline" data-spacefinder-type="model.dotcomrendering.pageElements.ImageBlockElement"><div id="img-8"><picture><source England.</span> Photograph: Alex Davidson/Getty Images</figcaption></figure></article><article id="block-6873c0698f088b778dd2a4f2"><header></header><p><strong>46th over: England 162-5 (Stokes 24, Smith 6) </strong>Jadeja bowls his fifth over, the ninth of spin in this innings. The only attacking strokes I can recall are sweeps, most of them unsuccessful; Stokes tries another and is hit on the pad outside the line.</p></article><article id="block-6873bf838f08a97237f2ddd5"><header></header><p><strong>45th over: England 159-5 (Stokes 23, Smith 4) </strong>Smith has started calmly, getting a long way forward to smother the spin whenever possible. Once he gets his eye in he will surely try to reverse the pressure. What England would give for a Gilchristian cameo today.</p></article><gu-island name="LiveBlogEpic" priority="feature" deferuntil="idle"
